الوجه الثاني : في الاعتراض هو أنا نقول : أنتم في مذهبكم ما استغنيتم عن تخصيص الشيء عن مثله ، فإن العالم وجد عن السبب الموجب له على هيئات مخصوصه تماثل نقائضها ، فلم اختص ببعض الوجوه ؟ ! واستحالة تمييز الشيء مثله فى الفعل أو فى اللزوم بالطبع أو بالضرورة لا تختلف عن فإن قلتم : إن النظام الكلى للعالم لا يمكن إلا على الوجه الذي وجد ، وإن العالم لو كان أصغر أو أكبر مما هو الآن عليه لكان لا يتم هذا النظام ، وكذا القول في عدد الأفلاك وعدد الكواكب ، وزعمتم أن الكبير يخالف الصغير ، والكثير يفارق القليل فما يراد منه ، فليست متماثلة بل هي مختلفة ، إلا أن القوة البشرية تضعف عن درك وجوه الحكمة فى مقاديرها وتفاصيلها ، وإنما تدرك الحكمة فى بعضها ، كالحكمة فى ميل فلك البروج عن معدل النهار ، والحكمة في الأوج والفلك الخارج عن المركز ، والأكثر لا يدرك السر فيها ، ولكن يعرف اختلافها ، ولا بعد في أن يتميز الشيء عن خلافه لتعلق نظام الأمر به، وأما الأوقات متشابهة قطعاً بالنسبة إلى الإمكان وإلى النظام ، ولا يمكن أن يدعى أنه لو خلق بعد ما خلق أو قبله بلحظة لما تصور النظام، فإن تماثل الأحوال يعلم بالضرورة : فنقول : نحن وإن كنا نقدر على معارضتكم بمثله في الأحوال إذ قال قائلون : خلقه في الوقت الذى كان الأصلح الخلق فيه ، لكنا لا نقتصر على هذه المقابلة ، بل نفرض على أصلكم تخصيصاً في موضعين لا يمكن أن يقدر فيهما اختلاف ؛ أحدهما اختلاف جهة الحركة ، والآخر تعيين موضع القطب في الحركة على المنطقة ما من (۱) • ويتصور أما القطب فبيانه أن السماء كرة متحركة على قطبين كأنهما ثابتان ، وكرة السماء متشابهة الأجزاء ، فإنها بسيطة ، لا سيما الفلك الأعلى الذي هو التاسع فإنه غير مركب (1) أصلا ، وهو متحرك على قطبين شمالي وجنوبي ، فنقول : نقطتين متقابلتين من النقط التي لا نهاية (٢) لها عندهم إلا أن يكونا ، هم ، هما القطبين ، فلم تعينت نقطتا الشمال والجنوب للقطبية والثبات ؟ ! ولم لم يكن خط المنطقة مارا بالنقتطين حتى يعود القطب إلى نقتطين متقابلتين على المنطقة ؟ ! فإن كان فى مقدار كبر السماء وشكلها حكمة ، فما الذي ميز محل القطب عن غيره ، حتى تعين لكونه قطباً، دون سائر الأجزاء والنقط ، وجميع أجزاء الكرة متساوية ؟ ! وهذا لا مخرج عنه وجميع النقط متماثلة ، فإن قيل : لعل الموضع الذى عليه نقطة القطب يفارق غيره بخاصية تناسب كونه محلاً للقطب حتى يثبت ، فكأنه لا يفارق مكانه وحيزه ووضعه أو ما يفرض إطلاقه عليه من الأسامى ؛ وسائر مواضع الفلك يتبدل بالدور وضعها من الأفلاك ، والقطب ثابت الوضع ، فلعل ذلك الموضع كان أولى بأن يكون ثابت الوضع من غيره . قلنا : ففى هذا تصريح بتفاوت أجزاء الكرة الأولى في الطبيعة ، وأنها ليست متشابهة الأجزاء ؛ وهو على خلاف أصلكم ، إذ أصل ما استدللتم به على لزوم
The second point: in objection, we say: You, in your doctrine, have not dispensed with specifying one thing over its like. For the world came into being from the necessitating cause in specific configurations whose opposites are similar; so why was it specified with some aspects? And the impossibility of distinguishing a thing from its like in action or in necessary consequence by nature or necessity does not differ. If you say: The overall system of the world is not possible except in the manner it exists; and if the world were smaller or larger than it now is, this system would not be complete; similarly regarding the number of spheres and planets; and you claim that the large differs from the small, and the many differs from the few, so they are not similar but different—except that human power falls short of grasping the aspects of wisdom in their magnitudes and details, but it grasps wisdom in some of them, like the wisdom in the inclination of the ecliptic from the celestial equator, and the wisdom in the apogee and the eccentric sphere; and most do not grasp the secret in them, but know their difference; and there is no harm in a thing being distinguished from its opposite due to the attachment of the order to it. But as for times, they are absolutely similar with respect to possibility and order; and it cannot be claimed that if He created after He created or before by a moment, the order would not be conceivable—for the similarity of states is known necessarily. So we say: We, although we are able to counter you with the same regarding states, as some say He created it at the time that was most appropriate for creation, we do not restrict ourselves to this rebuttal, but we posit upon your principle a specification in two points in which difference cannot be supposed: one is the difference in the direction of motion, and the other is the determination of the position of the pole in motion on the ecliptic. [garbled] And as for the pole, its explanation is that the heaven is a sphere moving on two poles as if they are fixed; and the sphere of heaven is similar in parts, for it is simple, especially the highest sphere which is the ninth, for it is not composite at all, and it moves on two poles, north and south. So we say: two points opposite each other from the points that are infinite (2) according to them, except that they are the poles. So why were the north and south points specified for polarity and fixity? And why did the ecliptic line not pass through the two points so that the pole would return to two opposite points on the ecliptic? If there is wisdom in the magnitude and shape of the heaven, what distinguished the place of the pole from others so that it became specified as a pole, to the exclusion of the rest of the parts and points, while all parts of the sphere are equal? There is no escape from this, and all points are similar. If it is said: Perhaps the place on which the pole point lies differs from others by a property that suits it as a place for the pole so that it is fixed; thus it does not leave its place, its space, its position, or whatever names one may apply to it; while the rest of the positions of the sphere change by rotation, their position relative to the spheres, and the pole has a fixed position; so perhaps that place was more worthy to have fixed position than others. We say: In this there is a declaration of the difference of the parts of the first sphere in nature, and that they are not similar in parts; and this is contrary to your principle, for the basis on which you argued for the necessity...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' position on the impossibility of distinguishing between equals. Ghazali begins his second objection by stating that the philosophers themselves cannot avoid specifying one thing over its equal. He points to the world: it has specific configurations (size, number of spheres, etc.) that could have been different but are not; this requires a specifier. The philosophers might respond that the overall system necessitates these specific quantities because any change would ruin the system, and even if we don't grasp all the wisdom, we know they differ. But Ghazali then attacks the case of times: all moments are exactly alike in possibility and order, so there is no reason why creation occurred at one time rather than another. He then introduces two specific cases where the philosophers face the problem: the direction of motion (not elaborated) and the determination of the celestial pole. Regarding the pole, he argues that the heavenly sphere (especially the ninth sphere) is simple and all its points are identical. Yet two opposite points are designated as fixed poles. Why those points? They could be anywhere. The philosophers might suggest that the pole's location has a special property that suits it, but Ghazali counters that this would imply that the sphere's parts are not actually identical, contradicting the philosophers' own principle that the heavens are uniform. Thus they fail to avoid the need for a specifying attribute.

Key Terms
قطب
فلك
تماثل
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The poles are naturally determined by the structure of the sphere without any specifier.
Correction: On a perfectly uniform sphere, no point is naturally a pole; the choice of specific points as poles requires a specifier.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of the philosophers' hypothetical answer that the pole location has a special property?
A) It confirms the uniformity of the sphere.
B) It implies the sphere's parts are not actually uniform.
C) It solves the problem without contradiction.
D) It shows the pole is determined by the ecliptic.

Key Takeaway
The need to specify the pole on a uniform sphere shows that even the heavens require a specifier, contradicting the philosophers' principle of uniformity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the regularity and uniformity in your own life—your daily routines, your habits, your relationships—do you ever pause to ask why things are exactly as they are? Or do you assume they are self-evident? What would it mean for you if every detail required a Specifier?
?
Imagine that your life, like the celestial sphere, appears uniform and self-sufficient. Yet there are specific points—your unique talents, your circumstances, your trials—that seem arbitrarily placed. How does Ghazali's argument challenge you to see these as signs of a purposeful Chooser rather than random chance?
?
If you truly believed that every specification in your life—your location, your family, your abilities—was chosen by a Wise Specifier, what would you need to change about how you live tomorrow? What assumption about your own autonomy would you have to surrender?

Ghazali's Question on Celestial Motion Directions
Ghazali poses the second objection about the direction of celestial motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's second objection regarding the cause of differing directions of celestial motion and his initial response.

Core Idea
Why do celestial spheres move in opposite directions? Ghazali asks for the cause.

In this passage, Ghazali presents his second required point (ilzām) against the philosophers. He questions why some spheres move east to west and others west to east, given that all directions are equally possible. A philosopher's hypothetical answer is given, but Ghazali's full response is cut short. This fragment illustrates his method of questioning causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the structure: question, hypothetical answer, beginning of reply.
2
Identify the key elements
Find Ghazali's question, the philosopher's response, and where Ghazali's own answer starts. Observe the footnote marker and the abrupt end.
The text ends at 'الفلك الأعلى'.
3
Reflect on the incompleteness
Consider why Ghazali's full argument is not here. What might he have said next? This missing part likely completes his refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإلزام الثانى : تعين جهة حركة الأفلاك ، بعضها من المشرق إلى المغرب، و بعضها بالعكس ، مع تساوى الجهات ، ما سببها ، وتساوى الجهات كتساوى الأوقات من غير فرق ؟ ! فإن قيل : لو كان الكل يدور من جهة واحدة ، لما تباينت أوضاعها ، ولم تحدث مناسبات الكواكب ، بالتثليث ، والتسديس ، والمقارنة ، وغير ذلك ، ولكان الكل على وضع واحد لا يختلف قط ، وهذه المناسبات مبدأ الحوادث في العالم قلنا : لسنا نلتزم عدم (۲) اختلاف جهة الحركة بل نقول : الفلك الأعلى
The second required point: The determination of the direction of motion of the spheres, some from east to west, and others in reverse, while the directions are equal. What is its cause? And the equality of directions is like the equality of times without any difference. If it is said: If all rotated in one direction, their positions would not differ, and the configurations of the planets, by triplicity, sextile, conjunction, and others, would not occur, and everything would be in one position never differing, and these configurations are the origin of events in the world. We say: We do not deny the difference of direction of motion, rather we say: The highest orb...
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection: the determination of the direction of motion of the celestial spheres. Some spheres move from east to west, others in the opposite direction, yet the directions are equivalent. Ghazali asks for the cause of this difference. He anticipates a possible response from the philosophers: if all spheres moved in the same direction, there would be no variation in their positions, and hence no astrological configurations (triplicities, sextiles, conjunctions) that are said to be the origin of events in the world. Ghazali begins his reply by stating that he does not deny the difference in direction, but the text cuts off at 'the highest orb', leaving his full response incomplete.

Misconception: Ghazali's question is about the fact of opposite motions rather than the reason for the specific direction of each sphere.
Correction: The passage shows Ghazali asks for the cause of the specific direction, not just the fact of difference.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' imagined response, what would happen if all spheres moved in the same direction?
A) The spheres would collide.
B) There would be no configurations of planets and no events in the world.
C) The poles would not be fixed.
D) Time would not exist.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's second objection questions the causality behind the chosen directions of celestial motion, pointing to a philosophical weakness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Ghazali points out that all directions are equally possible, yet each sphere moves in a specific direction. Consider one habit or belief in your life that you think is 'just the way things are.' Is it really without a cause? If there is a cause, is it one you have consciously chosen, or one that has been imposed? What does that reveal about your own will and responsibility before God?
?
The philosophers argued that opposite motions are necessary for planetary configurations which cause events. Do you sometimes explain away God's direct involvement in the world by pointing to secondary causes? When you experience a blessing or a trial, do you immediately recognize the hand of God, or do you attribute it to 'natural' causes? What would change if you saw every event as directly chosen by Him?

The First Objection: Spherical Shape and Specific Properties
Ghazali objects to the spherical shape argument by questioning specific properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's objection that even if the heavens are spherical due to simplicity, the philosophers cannot explain why specific properties are found in particular parts of the heavens.

Core Idea
Uniformity does not explain why specific properties are in specific places.

Imam Ghazali challenges the philosophers' argument for the spherical shape of the heavens. He accepts that the sphere may be the simplest shape, but he points out that this does not account for the specific properties found in particular parts of the heavens. This dilemma undermines their claim of uniform simplicity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the philosophers' argument
Read the passage and note that the philosophers claim the heavens are spherical because they are simple and the sphere is the simplest shape. This is the starting point of Ghazali's objection.
Ghazali does not reject the shape itself, but the reasoning behind it.
2
Follow Ghazali's dilemma
Ghazali presents a dilemma: either all parts of the heavens accept a given property or only one part does. If all do, why is that property specific to one part? If only one does, why don't the other similar parts also accept it?
This dilemma exposes the weakness in the philosophers' argument.
3
See the implication for divine action
Ghazali concludes that the only explanations for such specificity are arbitrary preference or a quality that differentiates. This shows that the philosophers cannot rely on simplicity alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كون السماء كرى الشكل أنها بسيط الطبيعة متشابهة لا تفاوت فيها ، وأبسط الأشكال الكرة ، فإن التربيع والتسديس وغيرهما يقتضى خروج زوايا وتفاوتها ، وذلك لا يكون إلا بأمر زائد على الطبع البسيط ، ولكنه وإن خالف مذهبكم فليس يندفع الإلزام به ، فإن السؤال في تلك الخاصية قائم إذ سائر الأجزاء هل كان قابلا تلك الخاصية أم لا ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم ، فلم اختصت الخاصية من بين المتشابهات ببعضها ؟ وإن قالوا : لم يكن ذلك إلا في ذلك الموضع ، وسائر الأجزاء لا تقبلها فنقول : سائر الأجزاء من حيث إنها جسم قابل للصور متشابهة بالضرورة ! وتلك الخاصية لا يستحقها ذلك الموضع لمجرد كونه جسما ولا بمجرد كونه سماء، فإن هذا المعنى يشاركه فيه سائر أجزاء السماء، فلا بد أن يكون تخصيصه به بتحكم أو بصفة من شأنها تخصيص الشيء عن مثله، وإلا فكما يستقيم لهم قولهم : إن الأحوال في قبول وقوع العالم فيها متساوية ! يستقيم لخصومهم قولهم : إن أجزاء السماء في قبول المعنى الذي لأجله صار ثبوت الوضع أولى به في تبدل الوضع متساوية؛ وهذا لا مخرج منه
That the heaven is spherical in shape [is claimed] because it is simple in nature, uniform with no difference, and the simplest of shapes is the sphere, for the square, the hexagon, and others require the emergence of angles and their variance, and that does not occur except by something additional to the simple nature. But even if it opposes your doctrine, the objection is not repelled by it, for the question about that particular property remains: do all the other parts accept that property or not? If they say: yes, then why was the property specific to some of the uniform things? And if they say: that does not occur except in that place, and the other parts do not accept it, we say: the other parts, insofar as they are bodies receptive to forms, are necessarily uniform! And that property is not deserved by that place merely for being a body, nor merely for being a heaven, for this meaning is shared by all other parts of the heaven. So its specification must be either by arbitrary decision or by a quality that specifies a thing from its like. Otherwise, just as their statement that the states regarding the receptivity of the occurrence of the world in them are equal is valid, so the statement of their opponents is valid: that the parts of the heaven regarding the receptivity of the meaning due to which the stability of position becomes more appropriate for it in the change of position are equal. And there is no escape from this.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is an objection to the philosophers' argument that the heavens are spherical because they are simple and the sphere is the simplest shape. Ghazali points out that even if that were true, the philosophers cannot explain why a particular part of the heaven (e.g., the part that has a certain property like a specific celestial motion) is singled out from other parts that are similar. He presents a dilemma: either all parts accept that property (so why only one?), or only that part accepts it (but then why, since all parts are similar bodies?). The only explanations are arbitrary preference or a specific quality that differentiates it. This undermines the philosophers' claim that the heavens are uniform and thus spherical.

Key Terms
كرى الشكل
بسيط الطبيعة
خاصية
تحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Ghazali is accepting the spherical shape of the heavens.
Correction: Ghazali is not accepting the shape; he is refuting the philosophers' argument for it. He shows that even if the shape were accepted, the problem of specific properties remains.

Checkpoint
What is Ghazali's main point in this objection?
A) The heavens are not spherical.
B) The philosophers cannot explain why a specific property is in a particular part of the heaven.
C) The simplest shape is not the sphere.
D) All parts of the heaven are different.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali shows that the philosophers' argument for spherical shape fails to explain the specificity of properties in the heavens.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the precise properties of the universe—like the exact shape of the heavens—do you ever pause to realize that they could have been different? If they are not necessary by nature, then who or what chose them to be this way? Are you comfortable resting your faith in an arbitrary decision or a conscious choice?
?
Ghazali shows that even the best rational arguments crumble when confronted with the question of specificity. Is there any area of your life where you rely on 'obvious' reasons without questioning their ultimate foundation? Will you allow this lesson to unsettle your assumptions and drive you to seek the real Giver of properties?
?
If the philosophers are forced to admit either arbitrary preference or a specifying quality, which do you lean toward when thinking about the world's details? And how does that choice affect your relationship with the Creator—is He actively involved in every specific property, or do you leave room for chance? What would you have to change in your daily thoughts to truly live out the answer?

The Second Objection: Direction of Celestial Motion
Ghazali questions why celestial spheres move in opposite directions given the equivalence of directions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali challenges the philosophers' claim that opposite celestial motions are necessary for planetary aspects, by arguing for the equivalence of directions.

Core Idea
Equivalent directions make opposite motions arbitrary.

Ghazali continues his critique of the philosophers' cosmology by questioning why celestial spheres move in opposite directions. Given that all directions are equivalent, there seems to be no rational necessity for assigning east-west versus west-east motion. This passage presents a dialectical exchange: the philosophers defend the necessity of opposite motions to produce planetary aspects, but Ghazali counters that the same variety could be achieved by reversing the assignments, leaving the choice unexplained.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: objection, philosophical response, Ghazali's counter, and a final analogy.
The passage uses technical terms for planetary aspects (tathlith, tasdis, muqarana).
2
Identify the core argument
Ghazali asserts that directions are equivalent, so the actual assignment of motions is arbitrary. Find where he states that reversing the motions would produce the same results.
3
Analyze the analogy with time
Ghazali compares the equivalence of directions to the equivalence of times, which the philosophers themselves accept. Trace this analogy and see how it strengthens his case.
4
Consider the philosophical reply and Ghazali's response
The philosophers claim opposite motions are needed for variety. Ghazali replies that the same variety can be achieved by swapping the directions. Why does he think this is a problem?
This exposes an inconsistency in their reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإلزام الثانى : تعين جهة حركة الأفلاك ، بعضها من المشرق إلى المغرب، و بعضها بالعكس ، مع تساوى الجهات ، ما سببها ، وتساوى الجهات كتساوى الأوقات من غير فرق ؟ فإن قيل : لو كان الكل يدور من جهة واحدة ، لما تباينت أوضاعها ، ولم تحدث مناسبات الكواكب ، بالتثليث ، والتسديس ، والمقارنة ، وغير ذلك ، ولكان الكل على وضع واحد لا يختلف قط ، وهذه المناسبات مبدأ الحوادث في العالم قلنا : لسنا نلتزم عدم اختلاف جهة الحركة بل نقول : الفلك الأعلى يتحرك من المشرق إلى المغرب والذي تحته بالعكس ، وكل ما يمكن تحصيله بهذا يمكن تحصيله بعكسه ، وهو أن يتحرك الأعلى من المغرب إلى المشرق ، وما تحته بالعكس في مقابلته فيحصل التفاوت ؛ وجهات الحركة بعد كونها دورية ، وبعد كونها متقابلة ، متساوية ؛ فلم تميزت جهة عن جهة تماثلها ؟ فإن قالوا : الجهتان متقابلتان متضادتان . فكيف تتساويان ؟ قلنا : هذا كقول القائل : التقدم والتأخر في وجود العالم متضادان، فكيف يدعى تساويهما ؟ وكما زعموا أنه يعلم تشابه الأوقات المختلفة بالنسبة إلى إمكان الوجود ، وإلى كل مصلحة يمكن فرضها في الوجود ، فكذلك يعلم تساوى الأحياز والأوضاع والأماكن والجهات ، بالنسبة إلى قبول الحركة وكل مصلحة تتعلق بها ، فإن ساعت لهم دعوى الاختلاف هذا التشابه ، كان الخصومهم دعوى الاختلاف في الأحوال والهيئات أيضاً
The second objection: The determination of the direction of the motion of the spheres, some from east to west and some from west to east, while the directions are equivalent – what is its cause? And the equivalence of directions is like the equivalence of times without difference. For if it is said: If all rotated in one direction, their positions would not differ, and the aspects of the planets (tathlith, tasdis, muqarana, etc.) would not occur, and all would be in a single state never changing, and these aspects are the origin of events in the world. We say: We do not commit to the absence of difference in the direction of motion. Rather, we say: the highest sphere moves from east to west and that below it opposite, and everything that can be achieved by this can be achieved by its opposite, namely that the highest moves from west to east and that below it opposite, thus difference occurs. And the directions of motion, being circular and opposite, are equivalent; so why is one direction distinguished from its similar? For if they say: The two directions are opposite and contrary, so how can they be equivalent? We say: This is like the saying of someone who says: Priority and posteriority in the existence of the world are opposites, so how can their equivalence be claimed? And just as they claim that they know the similarity of different times with respect to the possibility of existence and to every benefit that can be assumed in existence, so they know the equivalence of spaces, positions, places, and directions with respect to the receptivity of motion and every benefit related to it. If they allowed for themselves the claim of difference despite this similarity, then their opponents may also claim difference in states and configurations.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage contains Ghazali's second objection. He asks why the celestial spheres have different directions of motion when all directions are equivalent. The philosophers reply that different directions are necessary for the variety of planetary aspects that cause events. Ghazali counters that the same variety could be achieved by reversing the directions. He then argues that since the directions are equivalent (just as times are equivalent), there is no reason to differentiate one from another. He compares it to the philosophers' own claim that times are equivalent for the possibility of existence; similarly, directions are equivalent for motion. So if they allow a difference in directions despite equivalence, their opponents can also claim differences in other uniform states.

Key Terms
جهة حركة
تساوى الجهات
تثليث
تسديس
مقارنة
أفلاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ghazali denies the actual motions or that he is proposing an alternative cosmology.
Correction: Ghazali is not denying the observed motions; he is attacking the rational necessity claimed by the philosophers. He argues that the specific assignment is arbitrary given equivalence.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali say about the possibility of reversing the motions?
A) It would cause chaos.
B) It would achieve the same variety of planetary aspects.
C) It is impossible.
D) The philosophers already accept it.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali forces the philosophers to admit that the specific assignment of celestial motions is arbitrary, undermining their claim of rational necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a conviction you hold about how the world works—something you believe 'must be this way.' After reading this passage, are you willing to consider that your belief might be based on familiarity rather than necessity? What would it mean for you to surrender that assumption to Allah's will?
?
When you look at the order of the universe, do you silently attribute it to natural laws as if they were self-sufficient? This passage challenges that. Ask yourself: where in your daily life do you rely on 'it has to be this way' instead of recognizing that every detail is held in being by Allah's free choice? What might change if you internalized that?
?
If the specific direction of celestial motion is arbitrary (from a rational standpoint), then the entire cosmic order depends on the sheer will of Allah. Does this thought unsettle you or comfort you? Be honest: does your heart prefer a universe that runs on predictable laws, or one that is at every moment subject to the active will of its Creator? How would you live differently if you truly felt the latter?

The Third Objection: Forcing a First Event from the Eternal
Ghazali argues that the philosophers must admit a first temporal event from an eternal being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the philosophers must admit a first temporal event from an eternal being, and their counter-objection concerning the lack of a factor differentiating the first event.

Core Idea
The chain of events forces a first temporal act from the Eternal.

In this passage, Ghazali turns the philosophers' own causal reasoning against them. They insist an eternal being cannot produce a temporal event, but Ghazali shows that the regress of events must end at an eternal cause, implying a first temporal effect. He then anticipates their objection that only the first event is problematic due to the absence of any external factor that could determine its moment of occurrence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly. Then read the literal translation. Notice the flow of the argument: Ghazali states his objection, then presents an anticipated reply.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the objection is not fully completed here.
2
Identify Ghazali's core argument
Locate the part where Ghazali argues that the chain of events cannot go on infinitely, so it must end at an eternal being. This forces a first event from that eternal being.
Key phrase: 'لابد لكم من الاعتراف به' – you must admit it.
3
Analyze the philosophers' objection
Find where the philosophers reply: they do not reject any event from an eternal being, only the first event, because nothing distinguishes its moment of occurrence.
Note the list of factors that could differentiate: time, instrument, condition, etc.
4
Reflect on the dialectical purpose
Ask yourself: Why is Ghazali presenting this? He is not agreeing with the philosophers; he is using their own assumptions to show they must accept something they consider impossible.
This is a classic argument in the Tahafut tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض الثاني : على أصل دليلهم أن يقال : استبعدتم حدوث حادث من قديم ، ولابد لكم من الاعتراف به ، فإن في العالم حوادث ولها أسباب ، فإن استندت الحوادث إلى الحوادث إلى غير نهاية ، فهو محال ، وليس ذلك معتقد عاقل ، ولو كان ذلك ممكناً لاستغنيتم عن الاعتراف بالصانع وإثبات واجب وجود هو مستند الممكنات ، وإذا كانت الحوادث لها طرف ينتهي إليه سلسلتها ، فيكون ذلك الطرف هو القديم ، فلابد إذن على أصلكم من تجويز صدور حادث من قديم . فإن قيل : نحن لا نبعد صدور حادث عن قديم أي حادث كان ، بل نبعد صدور حادث هو أول الحوادث من القديم ، إذ لا يفارق حال الحدوث ما قبله في ترجيح جهة الوجود ، لا من حيث حضور وقت ولا آلة ولا شرط ولا طبيعة ولا غرض ولا سبب من سبب من الأسباب ، فأما إذا لم يكن هو الحادث الأول.
The second objection: Regarding the basis of their proof, it is said: You have considered improbable the occurrence of an event from an eternal being, but you must acknowledge it, for in the world there are events and they have causes. If events depend on events ad infinitum, that is impossible, and no rational person believes that. And if that were possible, you would have no need to acknowledge the Maker and to prove a Necessary Existence which is the support of contingent things. And since events have an end to which their chain terminates, then that end is the eternal. Therefore, according to your principle, it is necessary to allow the occurrence of an event from an eternal being. For if it is said: We do not deem improbable the occurrence of any event from an eternal being; rather, we deem improbable the occurrence of an event that is the first of events from the eternal, for the state of occurrence does not differ from what precedes it in the preponderance of the side of existence – neither in terms of a time, nor an instrument, nor a condition, nor a nature, nor an end, nor any cause whatsoever. But if it is not the first event...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents Ghazali's third objection against the philosophers' principle that an eternal being cannot produce a temporal event. Ghazali argues that the philosophers must accept that there is a first temporal event derived from an eternal being because the chain of causes must end at an eternal cause. If they object that only a first event is problematic because no external factor could differentiate the moment of occurrence, Ghazali seems to be cutting off, but the implication is that this objection is not valid.

Misconception: One might think Ghazali is endorsing the philosophers' view that an eternal being cannot produce a temporal event.
Correction: Ghazali is using their own principles to force them into a contradiction, not agreeing with their position.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali claim the philosophers must admit?

B) That there is no eternal being.
C) That a first event occurs from an eternal being.

Ghazali forces the philosophers to concede that an eternal being must produce a first temporal event on pain of infinite regress.

?

?

What 'preponderating factors' do you look for in your own life before trusting God? Are you waiting for a sign, a condition, or a perfect moment before submitting to His decree? Ghazali's Objection: The Problem of Equivalent Directions
Ghazali questions the differentiation of equal opposing directions in celestial motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's objection to the falasifa's argument for the uniqueness of celestial motions based on the equivalence of directions.

Core Idea
If directions are equivalent, why choose one over another?

This passage is a classic example of Ghazali's method of refutation by internal inconsistency. He takes the falasifa's own principles—that things equivalent in possibility should not be distinguished without a differentiator—and applies them to their account of celestial motion. The result is a powerful objection that questions the very basis of their cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the flow of the argument. Notice the back-and-forth structure between Ghazali and the falasifa.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify Ghazali's objection
Find where Ghazali states that directions are equivalent and then asks why one is distinguished over another. This is the core of his objection.
3
Analyze Ghazali's reply to the falasifa's counter
The falasifa claim directions are opposites, so not equivalent. Ghazali responds with an analogy about time, showing inconsistency in their reasoning.
This reveals Ghazali's strategy of demonstrating internal contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتحرك من المشرق إلى المغرب والذي تحته بالعكس ، وكل ما يمكن تحصيله بهذا يمكن تحصيله بعكسه ، وهو أن يتحرك الأعلى من المغرب إلى المشرق ، وما تحته بالعكس في مقابلته فيحصل التفاوت ؛ وجهات الحركة بعد كونها دورية ، وبعد كونها متقابلة ، متساوية ; فلم تميزت جهة عن جهة تماثلها ؟ ! فإن قالوا : الجهتان متقابلتان متضادتان . فكيف تتساويان ؟ ! قلنا : هذا كقول القائل : التقدم والتأخر فى وجود العالم متضادان، فكيف يدعى تساويهما ؟ ! وكما زعموا أنه يعلم تشابه الأوقات المختلفة بالنسبة إلى إمكان الوجود ، وإلى كل مصلحة يمكن فرضها في الوجود ، فكذلك يعلم (۱) تساوى الأحياز والأوضاع والأماكن والجهات ، بالنسبة إلى قبول الحركة وكل مصلحة تتعلق بها ، فإن ساعت لهم دعوى الاختلاف هذا التشابه ، كان الخصومهم دعوى الاختلاف فى الأحوال والهيئات أيضاً
It moves from east to west and what is below it moves in reverse, and everything that can be obtained by this can be obtained by its opposite, namely that the upper moves from west to east and what is below it moves in reverse opposite to it, so differentiation occurs. And the directions of motion, while being circular and while being opposite, are equivalent. Why then is one direction distinguished from its like? If they say: The two directions are opposites, so how can they be equivalent? We say: This is like the statement: 'Precedence and posteriority in the existence of the world are opposites, so how can their equivalence be claimed?' And just as they claim that he knows the similarity of different times with respect to the possibility of existence and to every benefit that can be supposed in existence, so too he knows(1) the equivalence of spaces, positions, places, and directions with respect to the reception of motion and every benefit connected to it. So if they are allowed the claim of difference in this similarity, then their opponents also have the claim of difference in states and configurations as well.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the falasifa's argument for the uniqueness of celestial motions. Ghazali argues that if directions are equivalent, there is no reason for one to be chosen over another. The falasifa respond that the directions are opposites, hence not equivalent, but Ghazali replies by analogy with priority and posteriority in time, which are also opposites yet the falasifa claim their equivalence. This shows inconsistency in their reasoning.

Key Terms
حركة دورية
جهات
متقابلة
متساوية
إمكان الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The falasifa's claim that opposite directions cannot be equivalent because they are opposites is a valid objection.
Correction: Ghazali shows via analogy with time that being opposites does not preclude equivalence in possibility, as the falasifa themselves accept for time.

Checkpoint
What is Ghazali's main objection in this passage?
A) That celestial motions are impossible
B) That if directions are equivalent, there is no reason for one to be chosen over another
C) That the falasifa deny the equivalence of directions
D) That the upper sphere should not move

Key Takeaway
Ghazali uses the falasifa's own premise of equivalence to show that their explanation of celestial motion is inconsistent.

?

Are you willing to scrutinize your own assumptions about God's actions? Pray that He grants you the courage to see the truth.

Ghazali's Challenge: The First Temporal Event Must Originate from the Eternal
Ghazali's objection and the falasifa's initial distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the falasifa must acknowledge a temporal event originating from an eternal being, and their initial response limiting this to the first event.

Core Idea
Ghazali forces the falasifa to admit that the eternal can produce a temporal event.

In this passage, Ghazali presents his second objection against the falasifa's cosmology. He argues that because temporal events exist and an infinite regress is impossible, the chain of causes must end with an eternal cause. The falasifa respond by denying only the very first temporal event, allowing later events through intermediaries. Let's examine this dialectical exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how Ghazali structures his argument: temporal events exist, their causes cannot regress infinitely, so they must end at an eternal.
2
Identify the logical structure
Break Ghazali's argument into premises and conclusion. What are the key premises? (temporal events have causes, infinite regress is impossible, chain must end).
3
Examine the falasifa's response
The falasifa distinguish between the first temporal event and subsequent ones. Why do they only deny the first? What do they allow for later events?
Notice their use of 'preparation of the receptive substrate' and 'suitable time'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض الثاني : على أصل دليلهم أن يقال : استبعدتم حدوث حادث من قديم ، ولابد لكم من الاعتراف به ، فإن فى العالم حوادث ولها أسباب ، فإن استندت الحوادث إلى الحوادث إلى غير نهاية ، فهو محال ، وليس ذلك معتقد عاقل ، ولو كان ذلك ممكناً لاستغنيتم عن الاعتراف بالصانع وإثبات واجب وجود هو مستند الممكنات ، و إذا كانت الحوادث لها طرف ينتهى إليه سلسلتها ، فيكون ذلك الطرف هو القديم ، فلابد إذن على أصلكم من تجويز صدور حادث من قديم . فإن قيل : نحن لا نبعد صدور حادث عن قديم أى حادث كان ، بل نبعد صدور حادث هو أول الحوادث من القديم ، إذ لا يفارق حال الحدوث ما قبله في ترجيح جهة الوجود ، لا من حيث حضور وقت ولا آلة ولا شرط ولا طبيعة ولا غرض ولا سبب من سبب من الأسباب ، فأما إذا لم يكن هو الحادث الأول. جاز يصدر منه عند حدوث شيء آخر من استعداد المحل القابل وحضور الوقت الموافق أو ما يجرى هذا المجرى . قلنا : فالسؤال فى حصول الاستعداد وحضور الوقت وكل ما يتجدد ، قائم . فإما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية أو ينتهى إلى قديم يكون أول حادث منه . فإن قيل : المواد القابلة للصور والأعراض والكيفيات ليس شيء منها حادثاً . والكيفيات الحادثة هي حركة الأفلاك ، أعنى الحركة الدورية وما يتجدد من الأوصاف الإضافية لها ، من التثليث والتربيع والتسديس ، وهي نسبة بعض أجزاء الفلك والكواكب إلى بعض ، وبعضها نسبة إلى الأرض ، كما يحصل من الطلوع والشروق والزوال عن منتهى الارتفاع ، والبعد عن الأرض يكون الكوكب في الأوج ، والقرب بكونه فى الحضيض ، والميل عن بعض الأقطار بكونه في الشمال والجنوب ؛ وهذه الإضافة لازمة للحركة الدورية بالضرورة ، فموجبها الحركة الدورية ; وأما الحوادث فيما يحويه مقعر فلك القمر ، وهو العناصر الأربعة ، بما يعرض فيها من كون وفساد ، وامتزاج وافتراق ، واستحالة من صفة إلى صفة ، فكل ذلك حوادث مستند بعضها إلى بعض في تفصيل طويل ، و بالآخرة تنتهى مبادئ أسبابها إلى الحركة السماوية الدورية ، ونسب الكواكب بعضها إلى بعض أو نسبتها إلى الأرض فيخرج من مجموع ذلك أن الحركة الدورية الدائمة الأبدية ، مستند الحوادث كلها ، ومحرك السماء حركتها الدورية نفوس السموات ، فإنها حية نازلة منزلة نفوسنا بالنسبة إلى أبداننا ، ونفوسها قديمة ، فلا جرم أن الحركة الدورية التى هى موجبها أيضاً قديمة ، ولما تشابهت أحوال النفس لكونها قديمة ، تشابهت أحوال الحركات ، أي كانت دائرة أبداً فإذن لا يتصور أن يصدر الحادث من قديم إلا بواسطة حركة دورية ، تشبه القديم من وجه ، فإنه دائم أبداً ، وتشبه الحادث من وجه ، فإن أبدية كل جزء يفرض منها ، كان حادثاً بعد أن لم يكن ، فهو (١) من حيث إنه
The second objection: On the basis of their argument it is said: You have deemed improbable the occurrence of a temporal event from the eternal, yet you must acknowledge it, for in the world there are temporal events and they have causes. If the temporal events are traced back to temporal events ad infinitum, that is impossible, and no rational person holds that. And if that were possible, you would have dispensed with acknowledging the Maker and establishing the Necessary Existence who is the support of contingent things. And since temporal events have a limit at which their chain ends, that limit is the eternal. Therefore, according to your own principle, you must allow the occurrence of a temporal event from the eternal. If it is said: We do not deem improbable the occurrence of any temporal event from the eternal; rather, we deem improbable the occurrence of a temporal event that is the first of temporal events from the eternal, for the state of occurrence is not distinguished from what preceded it in preferring the side of existence, neither by the presence of a time, nor an instrument, nor a condition, nor a nature, nor a purpose, nor any cause of the causes. But if it is not the first temporal event, it is possible for it to occur from it when another thing occurs, such as the preparation of the receptive substrate and the coming of the suitable time, or what is of this kind. We say: The question about the occurrence of the preparation and the coming of the time and everything that is renewed remains. Either it leads to an infinite regress or it ends with an eternal that is the first temporal event from it. If it is said: The materials receptive of forms, accidents, and qualities are not temporal at all. The temporal qualities are the motion of the spheres, that is, circular motion, and what is renewed of its additional attributes, such as trine, square, and sextile aspects, which are the ratios of some parts of the celestial sphere and planets to others, and some of their ratios to the earth, as occurs from rising, setting, culmination, and distance from the earth when the planet is in apogee, or proximity when it is in perigee, and inclination from some regions when it is in the north or south. These attributes are necessarily concomitant with circular motion, so their cause is circular motion. As for the temporal events in what is contained by the concave surface of the lunar sphere, namely the four elements, including what occurs in them of generation and corruption, mixing and separation, and change from one quality to another, all these are temporal events, some dependent on others in a long detail, and ultimately the principles of their causes end with the perpetual circular motion and the ratios of the planets to each other or to the earth. Thus from all this it emerges that the perpetual eternal circular motion is the support of all temporal events. The mover of the heaven in its circular motion is the souls of the heavens, for they are living, analogous to our souls in relation to our bodies, and their souls are eternal. Hence the circular motion which is their effect is also eternal. And since the states of the soul are uniform because it is eternal, the states of the motions are uniform, meaning they are perpetually circular. Therefore, it is inconceivable that a temporal event should proceed from the eternal except by means of a circular motion which resembles the eternal in one respect, for it is perpetually eternal, and resembles the temporal in another respect, for the eternity of each part that is supposed from it is temporal after having been non-existent. So it (the motion) is, in that it...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is the second objection and its response. Ghazali begins by pointing out that the falasifa must admit the occurrence of a temporal event from an eternal being, because temporal events exist, their chain of causes cannot go back infinitely, and must end with an eternal cause. The falasifa respond that they only deny the first temporal event; later events can occur through intermediates like the preparation of matter and suitable time. Ghazali retorts that the same question applies to these intermediates, leading to an infinite regress or a first temporal event. The falasifa then elaborate their cosmology: the ultimate temporal events depend on the eternal circular motion of the heavens, which is caused by eternal souls. The circular motion is both eternal (as a whole) and temporal (in its parts), and thus serves as a bridge. Ghazali's objection is that this does not truly solve the problem, as the origin of the motion itself remains unexplained.

Key Terms
حادث
قديم
استعداد
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The falasifa deny that any temporal event can come from the eternal.
Correction: The falasifa only deny the first temporal event; they allow later events through intermediates.

Checkpoint
According to the falasifa's response, when can a temporal event originate from the eternal?
A) Only if it is the first temporal event
B) Only if it is not the first temporal event and there is an intermediate like preparation of matter
C) At any time, directly from the eternal
D) Never, because the eternal cannot produce anything temporal

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's objection forces the falasifa to concede that temporal events must ultimately originate from the eternal, but they restrict this to events that are not the very first.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that every temporal event must have a cause, and the chain ends in the Eternal. Do you live as if your daily actions are merely random, or do you acknowledge that each moment is sustained by the Eternal? How would your life change if you truly felt the weight of that dependence?
?
The falasifa distinguished between the first event and subsequent events to protect their philosophy. In what area of your life do you make similar distinctions to avoid acknowledging the direct role of the Eternal? What would it cost you to admit that He is involved in every detail, not just the 'first cause'?
?
If every cause ultimately traces back to the Eternal, then your next thought, your next breath, is a direct gift from Him. How does that change your sense of accountability? Will you live today as if every action is seen and sustained by the One who caused the first event?

The Falasifa's Cosmology: Circular Motion as the Bridge
The falasifa's explanation of temporal events via eternal circular motion and souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the falasifa use eternal circular motion and celestial souls to explain the origination of temporal events from the eternal, addressing Ghazali's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Circular motion bridges the eternal and temporal by being perpetual yet composed of temporal parts.

After Ghazali's counter that the same problem applies to the intermediaries (preparation, time), the falasifa elaborate a detailed cosmological model. They argue that temporal events ultimately depend on the eternal circular motion of the heavens, which is caused by eternal souls. This motion, being both eternal in its continuity and temporal in its parts, serves as the necessary intermediate. Let's explore their response.

Guided Path
1
Read the falasifa's detailed explanation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how they build the causal chain: from eternal souls to circular motion to temporal events in the sublunary world.
2
Understand the role of circular motion
Why is circular motion special? It is eternal as a whole, but each part of it is temporal. This duality allows it to mediate between the eternal and temporal.
3
Grasp the role of celestial souls
The souls of the heavens are eternal and cause the circular motion. Since the soul is uniform, the motion is uniform and perpetual.

الاعتراض الثاني : على أصل دليلهم أن يقال : استبعدتم حدوث حادث من قديم ، ولابد لكم من الاعتراف به ، فإن فى العالم حوادث ولها أسباب ، فإن استندت الحوادث إلى الحوادث إلى غير نهاية ، فهو محال ، وليس ذلك معتقد عاقل ، ولو كان ذلك ممكناً لاستغنيتم عن الاعتراف بالصانع وإثبات واجب وجود هو مستند الممكنات ، و إذا كانت الحوادث لها طرف ينتهى إليه سلسلتها ، فيكون ذلك الطرف هو القديم ، فلابد إذن على أصلكم من تجويز صدور حادث من قديم . فإن قيل : نحن لا نبعد صدور حادث عن قديم أى حادث كان ، بل نبعد صدور حادث هو أول الحوادث من القديم ، إذ لا يفارق حال الحدوث ما قبله في ترجيح جهة الوجود ، لا من حيث حضور وقت ولا آلة ولا شرط ولا طبيعة ولا غرض ولا سبب من سبب من الأسباب ، فأما إذا لم يكن هو الحادث الأول. جاز يصدر منه عند حدوث شيء آخر من استعداد المحل القابل وحضور الوقت الموافق أو ما يجرى هذا المجرى . قلنا : فالسؤال فى حصول الاستعداد وحضور الوقت وكل ما يتجدد ، قائم . فإما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية أو ينتهى إلى قديم يكون أول حادث منه . فإن قيل : المواد القابلة للصور والأعراض والكيفيات ليس شيء منها حادثاً . والكيفيات الحادثة هي حركة الأفلاك ، أعنى الحركة الدورية وما يتجدد من الأوصاف الإضافية لها ، من التثليث والتربيع والتسديس ، وهي نسبة بعض أجزاء الفلك والكواكب إلى بعض ، وبعضها نسبة إلى الأرض ، كما يحصل من الطلوع والشروق والزوال عن منتهى الارتفاع ، والبعد عن الأرض يكون الكوكب في الأوج ، والقرب بكونه فى الحضيض ، والميل عن بعض الأقطار بكونه في الشمال والجنوب ؛ وهذه الإضافة لازمة للحركة الدورية بالضرورة ، فموجبها الحركة الدورية ; وأما الحوادث فيما يحويه مقعر فلك القمر ، وهو العناصر الأربعة ، بما يعرض فيها من كون وفساد ، وامتزاج وافتراق ، واستحالة من صفة إلى صفة ، فكل ذلك حوادث مستند بعضها إلى بعض في تفصيل طويل ، و بالآخرة تنتهى مبادئ أسبابها إلى الحركة السماوية الدورية ، ونسب الكواكب بعضها إلى بعض أو نسبتها إلى الأرض فيخرج من مجموع ذلك أن الحركة الدورية الدائمة الأبدية ، مستند الحوادث كلها ، ومحرك السماء حركتها الدورية نفوس السموات ، فإنها حية نازلة منزلة نفوسنا بالنسبة إلى أبداننا ، ونفوسها قديمة ، فلا جرم أن الحركة الدورية التى هى موجبها أيضاً قديمة ، ولما تشابهت أحوال النفس لكونها قديمة ، تشابهت أحوال الحركات ، أي كانت دائرة أبداً فإذن لا يتصور أن يصدر الحادث من قديم إلا بواسطة حركة دورية ، تشبه القديم من وجه ، فإنه دائم أبداً ، وتشبه الحادث من وجه ، فإن أبدية كل جزء يفرض منها ، كان حادثاً بعد أن لم يكن ، فهو (١) من حيث إنه
The second objection: On the basis of their argument it is said: You have deemed improbable the occurrence of a temporal event from the eternal, yet you must acknowledge it, for in the world there are temporal events and they have causes. If the temporal events are traced back to temporal events ad infinitum, that is impossible, and no rational person holds that. And if that were possible, you would have dispensed with acknowledging the Maker and establishing the Necessary Existence who is the support of contingent things. And since temporal events have a limit at which their chain ends, that limit is the eternal. Therefore, according to your own principle, you must allow the occurrence of a temporal event from the eternal. If it is said: We do not deem improbable the occurrence of any temporal event from the eternal; rather, we deem improbable the occurrence of a temporal event that is the first of temporal events from the eternal, for the state of occurrence is not distinguished from what preceded it in preferring the side of existence, neither by the presence of a time, nor an instrument, nor a condition, nor a nature, nor a purpose, nor any cause of the causes. But if it is not the first temporal event, it is possible for it to occur from it when another thing occurs, such as the preparation of the receptive substrate and the coming of the suitable time, or what is of this kind. We say: The question about the occurrence of the preparation and the coming of the time and everything that is renewed remains. Either it leads to an infinite regress or it ends with an eternal that is the first temporal event from it. If it is said: The materials receptive of forms, accidents, and qualities are not temporal at all. The temporal qualities are the motion of the spheres, that is, circular motion, and what is renewed of its additional attributes, such as trine, square, and sextile aspects, which are the ratios of some parts of the celestial sphere and planets to others, and some of their ratios to the earth, as occurs from rising, setting, culmination, and distance from the earth when the planet is in apogee, or proximity when it is in perigee, and inclination from some regions when it is in the north or south. These attributes are necessarily concomitant with circular motion, so their cause is circular motion. As for the temporal events in what is contained by the concave surface of the lunar sphere, namely the four elements, including what occurs in them of generation and corruption, mixing and separation, and change from one quality to another, all these are temporal events, some dependent on others in a long detail, and ultimately the principles of their causes end with the perpetual circular motion and the ratios of the planets to each other or to the earth. Thus from all this it emerges that the perpetual eternal circular motion is the support of all temporal events. The mover of the heaven in its circular motion is the souls of the heavens, for they are living, analogous to our souls in relation to our bodies, and their souls are eternal. Hence the circular motion which is their effect is also eternal. And since the states of the soul are uniform because it is eternal, the states of the motions are uniform, meaning they are perpetually circular. Therefore, it is inconceivable that a temporal event should proceed from the eternal except by means of a circular motion which resembles the eternal in one respect, for it is perpetually eternal, and resembles the temporal in another respect, for the eternity of each part that is supposed from it is temporal after having been non-existent. So it (the motion) is, in that it...
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is the second objection and its response. Ghazali begins by pointing out that the falasifa must admit the occurrence of a temporal event from an eternal being, because temporal events exist, their chain of causes cannot go back infinitely, and must end with an eternal cause. The falasifa respond that they only deny the first temporal event; later events can occur through intermediates like the preparation of matter and suitable time. Ghazali retorts that the same question applies to these intermediates, leading to an infinite regress or a first temporal event. The falasifa then elaborate their cosmology: the ultimate temporal events depend on the eternal circular motion of the heavens, which is caused by eternal souls. The circular motion is both eternal (as a whole) and temporal (in its parts), and thus serves as a bridge. Ghazali's objection is that this does not truly solve the problem, as the origin of the motion itself remains unexplained.

حركة دورية
نفوس السموات
حادث
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The falasifa believe temporal events come directly from the eternal without any mediation.
Correction: They argue that temporal events require an intermediate — eternal circular motion — which is both eternal and temporal.

Checkpoint
According to the falasifa, what is the ultimate support of all temporal events?
A) The direct will of the eternal
B) The material elements themselves
C) The perpetual circular motion of the heavens
D) The souls of individual humans

Key Takeaway
The falasifa use eternal circular motion, caused by eternal souls, as a bridge to explain how temporal events can originate from the eternal, addressing Ghazali's objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The falasifa argue that the eternal cannot directly produce temporal events without a bridge. Do you live as though you need intermediaries—such as your own skills, status, or routines—to receive what only God can give directly? What would it mean for your daily reliance on Him if you truly believed He can create from nothing without any means?
?
The souls of the heavens are described as eternal and uniform, producing a motion that never changes. In contrast, your own soul is created and constantly changing. When you reflect on your desires, decisions, and spiritual states, do you act as if your soul is self-sufficient and independent, or do you recognize that every moment of existence and stability is a gift from God? How would this recognition change the way you pray, work, and relate to others today?
?
Each part of circular motion is temporal—it comes and goes. Consider your own actions: they are temporal events that appear and vanish. Do you truly believe that each action is created directly by God at every instant, or do you implicitly rely on your own power and continuity? What would it look like to live with constant awareness that 'there is no power nor strength except with God' (lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh) in every single deed you do?

The Philosophers' Theory of Circular Motion as Mediator
Philosophers argue that circular motion mediates between eternal and temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' claim that perpetual circular motion is the necessary intermediary between the eternal and the temporal.

Core Idea
Perpetual motion is the philosophers' bridge between the eternal and the temporal.

In this passage, Ghazali presents the detailed argument of the philosophers who claim that temporal events can only proceed from the eternal through a perpetual circular motion. They attempt to show that the circular motion of the heavens, being both eternal in its continuity and temporal in its parts, serves as the necessary link. This lesson unpacks their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' exposition
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully to understand the full theory.
Notice the structure: initial problem, then their response.
2
Identify the key components
Notice how they distinguish between the eternal souls of the heavens, the perpetual motion, and the temporal events in the sublunary world.
3
Consider the role of relations
The philosophers rely on relational descriptions (trine, square, etc.) to explain how the motion produces temporal effects.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The philosophers conclude that circular motion is both eternal and temporal, thus mediating between the two.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جاز يصدر منه عند حدوث شيء آخر من استعداد المحل القابل وحضور الوقت الموافق أو ما يجرى هذا المجرى . قلنا : فالسؤال فى حصول الاستعداد وحضور الوقت وكل ما يتجدد ، قائم . فإما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية أو ينتهى إلى قديم يكون أول حادث منه . فإن قيل : المواد القابلة للصور والأعراض والكيفيات ليس شيء منها حادثاً . والكيفيات الحادثة هي حركة الأفلاك ، أعنى الحركة الدورية وما يتجدد من الأوصاف الإضافية لها ، من التثليث والتربيع والتسديس ، وهي نسبة بعض أجزاء الفلك والكواكب إلى بعض ، وبعضها نسبة إلى الأرض ، كما يحصل من الطلوع والشروق والزوال عن منتهى الارتفاع ، والبعد عن الأرض يكون الكوكب في الأوج ، والقرب بكونه فى الحضيض ، والميل عن بعض الأقطار بكونه في الشمال والجنوب ؛ وهذه الإضافة لازمة للحركة الدورية بالضرورة ، فموجبها الحركة الدورية ؛ وأما الحوادث فيما يحويه مقعر فلك القمر ، وهو العناصر الأربعة ، بما يعرض فيها من كون وفساد ، وامتزاج وافتراق ، واستحالة من صفة إلى صفة ، فكل ذلك حوادث مستند بعضها إلى بعض في تفصيل طويل ، و بالآخرة تنتهى مبادئ أسبابها إلى الحركة السماوية الدورية ، ونسب الكواكب بعضها إلى بعض أو نسبتها إلى الأرض فيخرج من مجموع ذلك أن الحركة الدورية الدائمة الأبدية ، مستند الحوادث كلها ، ومحرك السماء حركتها الدورية نفوس السموات ، فإنها حية نازلة منزلة نفوسنا بالنسبة إلى أبداننا ، ونفوسها قديمة ، فلا جرم أن الحركة الدورية التى هى موجبها أيضاً قديمة ، ولما تشابهت أحوال النفس لكونها قديمة ، تشابهت أحوال الحركات ، أي كانت دائرة أبداً فإذن لا يتصور أن يصدر الحادث من قديم إلا بواسطة حركة دورية ، تشبه القديم من وجه ، فإنه دائم أبداً ، وتشبه الحادث من وجه ، فإن أبدية كل جزء يفرض منها ، كان حادثاً بعد أن لم يكن ، فهي من حيث إنها حادث بأجزائه وإضافاته ، مبدأ الحوادث ومن حيث إنها أبدى متشابه الأحوال ، صادر عن نفس أزلية ؛ فإن كان في العالم حوادث فلا بد من حركة دورية ، وفى العالم حوادث ؛ فالحركة الدورية الأبدية ، ثابتة . المستند حادثة قلنا : هذا التطويل لا يغنيكم ، فإن الحركة الدورية التي هي أم قديمة ؟! فإن كانت قديمة فكيف صارت مبدأ لأول الحوادث ؟! وإن كانت حادثة افتقرت إلى حادث آخر ، وتسلسل الأمر ، وقولكم : إنه من وجه يشبه القديم ، ومن وجه يشبه الحادث، فإنه ثابت متجدد ، أي هو ثابت التجدد ، متجدد الثبوت فنقول : أهو مبدأ الحوادث من حيث إنه ثابت ، أو من حيث إنه متجدد ؟ ! فإن كان من حيث إنه ثابت ، فكيف صدر من ثابت متشابه الأحوال شيء في بعض الأوقات دون بعض ؟ ! وإن كان من حيث إنه متجدد ، فها سبب تجدده في نفسه ؟ ! فيحتاج إلى سبب آخر ويتسلسل فهذا غاية تقرير الإلزام ولهم في الخروج عن هذا الإلزام نوع احتيال سنورده في بعض المسائل بعد هذه ، كيلا يطول كلام هذه المسألة بانشعاب شجون الكلام وفنونه ، على أنا سنبين أن الحركة الدورية لا تصلح أن تكون مبدأ الحوادث ، فإن جميع الحوادث مخترعة لله ابتداء ، ونبطل ما قالوه : من كون السماء حيواناً متحركاً بالاختيار ، حركة نفسية كحركتنا
It may originate from Him when another thing occurs, such as the preparedness of the receptive substrate, the presence of the suitable time, or whatever runs in this course. We say: The question about the occurrence of preparedness, the presence of time, and everything that becomes new, remains. Either it goes on ad infinitum or it ends with an eternal being which is the first temporal thing from it. If it is said: The materials receptive of forms, accidents, and qualities are none of them temporal. The temporal qualities are the motion of the spheres, that is, the circular motion and what becomes new of their relational descriptions, such as trine, square, and sextile—these are the relation of some parts of the sphere and planets to others, and some of them relation to the earth, as occurs from rising, dawning, and departure from the maximum height, and distance from the earth causes the planet to be at apogee, and proximity causes it to be at perigee, and inclination from some regions causes it to be in the north or south; and this relation is necessarily concomitant with circular motion, so its cause is circular motion. As for the temporal events in what is contained by the concave of the sphere of the moon—that is, the four elements—including what occurs in them of generation and corruption, mixture and separation, and transformation from one attribute to another—all that is temporal events, some depending on others in a long detail, and ultimately the principles of their causes end at the celestial circular motion and the relations of the planets to each other or their relation to the earth. From all that it follows that the perpetual eternal circular motion is the basis of all temporal events. The mover of the heaven in its circular motion is the souls of the heavens, for they are living beings in the status of our souls relative to our bodies, and their souls are eternal; inevitably the circular motion which is their effect is also eternal. And since the states of the soul are similar because it is eternal, the states of the motions are similar, i.e., they were always circular eternally. Therefore, it is inconceivable that a temporal event should proceed from the eternal except through a circular motion which resembles the eternal in one respect—for it is perpetual eternally—and resembles the temporal in another respect—for the perpetuity of each part that one supposes of it is temporal, having come to be after it was not. So it is, insofar as it is temporal in its parts and relations, the principle of temporal events; and insofar as it is eternal and uniform in states, it proceeds from an eternal soul. If there are temporal events in the world, there must be a circular motion; and there are temporal events in the world; thus the eternal circular motion is established. Its basis is temporal? We say: This lengthy discourse does not avail you. For the circular motion—is it eternal or temporal?! If it is eternal, how did it become the principle of the first temporal event?! If it is temporal, it would require another temporal event, leading to infinite regress. And your statement that it resembles the eternal in one respect and the temporal in another—it is constant and renewing, i.e., it is constant in renewal, renewing in constancy. We say: Is it the principle of temporal events insofar as it is constant, or insofar as it is renewing?! If insofar as it is constant, how did something issue from a constant uniform state at some times and not others?! If insofar as it is renewing, then what is the cause of its renewal in itself?! It would need another cause, leading to infinite regress. This is the fullest presentation of the constraint. And they have a kind of subterfuge to escape this constraint, which we will present in some later questions, so that the discussion of this question does not become prolonged by the branching of its themes and varieties. Moreover, we will show that circular motion is not fit to be the principle of temporal events, for all temporal events are created by God from the beginning, and we will invalidate their claim that the heaven is an animal moving by choice, with a psychic motion like our motion.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a sustained argument and refutation. It begins with an implicit objection: it might be said that the eternal can give rise to a temporal event only when another temporal condition occurs (like preparedness or suitable time). Ghazali immediately counters: that condition itself is temporal, leading either to infinite regress or an eternal first temporal event. He then, in the voice of the philosophers, offers a detailed theory: the materials of the sublunary world are not themselves temporal; temporal qualities arise from the circular motion of the heavens and their relational descriptions (trine, square, etc.), which are necessary concomitants of that motion. All sublunary generation and corruption ultimately trace back to this perpetual circular motion. The motion is caused by the eternal souls of the heavens, which are like our souls but eternal. Because the soul is eternal, its effect (circular motion) is also eternal and uniform, yet each part of that motion is temporal, providing a link between the eternal and the temporal. Thus, the philosophers conclude, temporal events can only proceed from the eternal through such a motion. Ghazali then refutes this: if the circular motion is eternal, it cannot be the cause of the first temporal event, since an eternal cause would produce its effect eternally, not at a particular time. If it is temporal, it requires another cause, leading to infinite regress. The philosophers' claim that it is 'constant and renewing' fails because if it is constant, it cannot explain why a temporal event occurs at one time rather than another; if it is renewing, that renewal itself needs a cause. Ghazali concludes that this is a decisive refutation, though he postpones his own full demonstration that all temporal events are directly created by God and that the heaven is not a self-moving animal.

Key Terms
حركة دورية (circular motion)
نفوس السموات (souls of the heavens)
قديم (eternal)
حادث (temporal)

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that perpetual circular motion, being both eternal and temporal, is the only way temporal events can proceed from an eternal source.

Ghazali's Refutation: The Dilemma of Eternal or Temporal Motion
Ghazali refutes the philosophers' theory with a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's refutation of the philosophers' claim by showing the inherent contradiction in the notion of an intermediary that is both constant and renewing.

Core Idea
If circular motion is eternal, it cannot cause a first temporal event; if temporal, it requires another cause.

Having presented the philosophers' theory, Ghazali now delivers his refutation. He exposes a central dilemma: the circular motion cannot be both the principle of temporal events and the effect of an eternal cause without leading to absurdities. This lesson examines his incisive critique.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's objection
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the dilemma.
Pay attention to the two-part question: 'is it eternal or temporal?'
2
Analyze the two options
Ghazali asks: is the motion eternal or temporal? Each leads to a problem.
3
Examine the 'constant and renewing' claim
Ghazali challenges the philosophers' characterization by asking what aspect makes it the principle.
4
Understand the conclusion
Ghazali defers further discussion but asserts that circular motion is unfit and that all events are directly from God.
